23/09/2024, 15:20 - +254 700 517763: Advice as sought from Microsoft bing AI

Here are detailed control measures for managing grub larvae pests in coffee plants, specifically focusing on the Coffee Berry Borer (Hypothenemus hampei):

1. Cultural Control
Sanitation: Regularly remove and destroy infested berries from the plants and the ground. This helps reduce the pest population by eliminating breeding sites1.

Pruning: Prune coffee plants to improve air circulation and reduce humidity, which can make the environment less favorable for the pests2.

Shade Management: Properly manage shade trees to create an unfavorable environment for the Coffee Berry Borer3.

2. Biological Control
Natural Predators: Encourage or introduce natural predators such as ants and parasitic wasps (e.g., Phymastichus coffea) that can help control the Coffee Berry Borer population1.

Fungal Pathogens: Use entomopathogenic fungi like Beauveria bassiana, which can infect and kill the larvae and adult beetles2.

3. Chemical Control
Insecticides: Apply insecticides specifically labeled for use against coffee pests. It‚Äôs crucial to follow the recommended guidelines to minimize environmental impact and prevent resistance 
development3.

Traps: Use pheromone traps to monitor and reduce adult beetle populations. These traps can help in early detection and management of the pest4.

4. Integrated Pest Management (IPM)
Combination of Methods: Implement a coordinated approach that combines cultural, biological, and chemical control methods. This holistic strategy helps manage the pest population effectively while minimizing harm to the environment and non-target organisms4.

5. Monitoring and Early Detection
Regular Inspections: Conduct regular inspections of coffee plants to detect early signs of infestation. Early detection allows for timely intervention and reduces the spread of the pest1.

Pheromone Traps: Use pheromone traps to monitor the presence and activity of adult beetles. This helps in assessing the infestation level and planning control measures accordingly2.

6. Farmer Education and Training
Awareness Programs: Educate farmers about the importance of pest management practices and how to implement them effectively. Training programs can help farmers identify pests early and apply control measures correctly3.

06/10/2024, 08:21 - +254 795 220161: üåçüåçAttention: *All Coffee Farmers* 
 
 *MAJOR BEST AGRONOMIC PRACTICES(BAPs) FOR OCTOBER 2024.* 


[Thank you for reading this free newsletter. *Share*, distribute, and republish freely with credit to the source as 'Agronomist Dennis.'
For a personalized Coffee calendar and more details; For professional assistance on the WHAT, WHEN, WHERE and HOW on Coffee and the coffee value-chain in Kenya; For more free resources including tips on growing, production, and marketing, contact: *Agronomist Dennis, a Kenyan-Based Agronomist who may be contacted on (+254) 0795220161.* Agronomist Dennis Is A Champion For Farmers and Farming Communities in Kenya.]

The main challenge with most coffee farmers in the World is the ignorance of proper timing (the 'WHEN ") for the important agronomic practices.

Here are the major practices to do in your coffee farm this month:

 *MAJOR AGRONOMIC PRACTICES(BAPs) FOR OCTOBER 2024 IN COFFEE.* 

 *_Nutrition and Harvesting_* 

Farming is interesting and good yields are as a result of proper timing (the 'WHEN ') of application.Most farmers do forget or are not prepared or don't know when to apply what at what time.
Below is just a summary of the Do's to do in your coffee farm this month.

 *1.Nutrition* 
In our day to day life,we as human beings feed in a variety of foods as ugali,matoke,meat,greens  etc.Its boring taking one same meal over the weeks.I could rephrase this,how would you feel if you took githeri for a whole month?Will you like it?I don't think you may like it.
Just like we human beings,coffee requires a balanced fertiliser program for better yields and quality.

A balanced fertiliser program is as a result of soil test and analysis.It involves a combination of  products such as  NPK fertiliser,manure,lime application, foliar feeds such as that of Zinc and boron. 

Two weeks after the short rains of October/November its important applying NPK fertiliser and manure/organic fertilizer. Manure application is vital as it ensures good soil structure,good moisture and nutrients retention.
Apply 10L of manure or 250g-500g of organic fertilizer. 

NPK fertiliser-use at the recommended rates

 *2.Keeping records* 
It's very vital to keep record on labour costs,harvest.A record will guide on how much profit/loss we could be naking.

 *3.Desuckering* 
Remove all unwanted suckers before feeding your coffee.Otherwise,these will be alternate sinks for the nutrients.

4 *.Weeding* 
Weeds reduces the yields by half.Ensure you uproot under canopy,Slash between rows.
Herbicides usage may affect the quality of final bean as residues.Thus avoid them.

 *5.Harvesting* 
In most parts coffee has started ripening. It's important that as we pick,put in clean bucket and sacks,ensure the coffee does not get into contact with soil.Don't pick the overripe,or green berries.

 *Note:* 
‚óèUse of pesticides and fungicides at this stage would leave residues of chemicals in the final bean.Avoid these.Use other Integrated methods to control the pests and diseases.
‚óèIt's important you apply both fertilizer and manure in your farm two weeks after the rains.
‚óèUse of compost or manure regularly on your trees helps cut the rate of application and hence cost of NPK. 
‚óèAs a farmer, you will get the highest yields in an environmentally sustainable way if you use both composted manure, man-made fertilisers  as NPK ,foliars and lime.


Issued:October 6, 2024.


 *General Notice:* This material is for general information to a large audience. Thus, results vary. Always contact a professional for support based on your specific needs, requirements, and situation.

18/10/2024, 23:26 - +254 795 220161: SALVAGING COFFEE FARMS FROM EFFECT OF CLIMATE CHANGE 2024   & IN THE FUTURE.

Preventing coffee trees from drying up.(An effect of climate change)

The beauty of coffee farming is seeing the results-healthy ,vigorous-growing trees.

One year ago,a time like now ,I put down in an article with similar topic as this on how to adapt coffee farms to climate change.It mentioned that,at no instance can we stop climate from changing but we can adapt to it.(https://www.linkedin.com/posts/dennis-kinyua-938628266_coffee-climatechange-environmentalsustainability-activity-7114680768315990017-nrgT?utm_source=share&utm_medium=member_android).

Having visited about 42 coffee farmers in the course of the month.Having seeing posts  of farmers seeking advice on what to do with their drying coffee;pushes me to enlighten us on how to shun from this calamity.
This month we are always enjoying the short rains,applying fertiliser in our farms,our coffee ripening;but the opposite is happening with coffee trees drying up,no fatigation etc.The rain has delayed.

Below are BAPs you can use to adapt your coffee.:
1.Due to increase in temperatures
2.Due to increased rainfall.


 *How to adapt coffee farms to extreme dry conditions* . 

1.Manure/Organic fertiliser application 
These increase soil organic matter which facilitates retention of moisture in the soil.Apply during whrn soil is wet.
2.Mulching -Reduces evaporation rate thus much moisture is retained. 
3.Shade trees-Reduces evapotranspiration, thus increasing soil moisture.Also, leafs fall increases soil organic matter.
4.Irrigation
There is no harm in irrigating your coffee trees especially in extreme dry conditions. Will you watch out and wait for the coffee trees and berries to dry up?Don't question.
Just irrigate and safe the crop.Do drip irrigation.

 *How to adapt coffee farms to extreme rainy conditions* . 

1.Mulching-Reduces speed of surface run off and allows for easier infiltration.
2.Shade trees -Reduces the intensity of rain drops and their roots bind soil together.
3.Plant stabilising grasses on the edge of terraces.
4.Terracing on hill side.

NOTE
Click on the link to find more on climate change.
WE CANNOT STOP CLIMATE CHANGE WE CAN ONLY ADAPT TO IT. 

Issued on:18 October 2024

By Agronomist Dennis. 
(DENAZA AGROCONSULTANCY LTD
0795220161).

03/11/2024, 15:27 - +254 795 220161: *MAJOR BEST AGRONOMIC PRACTICES IN COFFEE  FOR NOVEMBER 2024.*

With the effects of climate change, the farmers have been waiting for the rains to apply manure manure and fertiliser in our farms. Its my hope that you as a coffee farmer have purchased manure enough for your trees and also fertiliser.

It's important we be aware that,feeding contributes the highest percentage of tonnes you get from your coffee farm.The size and quality of cherry too will be a determinant of what you feed the soil with.

The rains have began and its important we now fo this 2weeks after the rains fall down well(when the soil is moist and feeder roots are actively growing).

Also in some parts  the coffee has flowered hence the below practices will help.

The major agronomic practices for November 2024 includes:

1. Manure application-Manure should be well decomposed . Whether farmyard or compost.
This aids in water and nutrients retention by the soil.Put a debe/ half a debe per tree.

2. Fertilizer application.Its important you feed the coffee plant depending on the amount of coffee it holds.An NPK fertiliser is best for coffee.

3. Berry borer trap installation in the farm. 
In the warm regions Coffee Berry Borer tends to get into the ripe cherries.Thus as the coffee continues to ripen,have Berry Borer traps in your farm.

4. Weeding and mulching 
Weeding is important to reduce the risks of competition for nutrients with the coffee plant.Ensure no weeds under canopy.
After manure and fertiliser application ,mulch your coffee to facilitate moisture retention.

5.Foliar feeds -
Spray foliars high in zinc and Boron  for the coffee where pinheads have been formed. 
For pesticide spray,be cautious of the PHI. 

6. Composting -Its very important that you continue making compost heaps to use in your farms next year.
Use coffee pulp to make compost too.

 *7.Record keeping* 
It's very important to keep the records of yields per harvest,labour and transport costs.
Also record the type of fertiliser and amount applied per tree.

 *NOTE* :
‚óè Nutrition is very important in coffee farms.
‚óèKeeping records is a vital tool in the agribusiness of coffee.
‚óèA good parent will not deny her children food so is a coffee farmer to their coffee trees.
 
Issued :3, November 2024.

Issued by : Agronomist Dennis/Denaza
(0795220161)

05/11/2024, 23:50 - +254 701 641933: Manure application

Apply 1 - 2 debes of well-decomposed manure/coffee pulp once a year during the dry weather, a month before the rains
Dig a shallow furrow ring (4 ‚Äì 6‚Äù deep), 30cm wide, starting from the drip line towards the stem. Apply the manure and mix with soil
05/11/2024, 23:53 - +254 701 641933: Boron/Zinc application

Apply a foliar mixture of Zinc and Boron at the rate of 2 - 3kg of each per Ha (40 - 60 g of each/20 liters of water) 2 ‚Äì 3 months before the main flowering
05/11/2024, 23:53 - +254 701 641933: Zinc (Zn)                                        

It is the only known metallic plant hormone which: 

Boosts flower initiation and formation
Enhances fruit set and leaf size
Sets the inter-nodal spacing on the branch and the stem
Enhances phosphorus uptake and utilization
Determines the leaf symmetry
Boron (B)                                                     

Enables flower fertilization by facilitating pollen germination through the stigma to the ovary.  Consequently, optimal flowering and fruit set are realized i.e. it minimizes flower abortion
Manages the utilization of water in the plant together with potassium.  Consequently, it regulates the uptake of water from the soil together with potassium
Promotes shoot and root growth
Facilitates protein and sugar synthesis from glucose

20/11/2024, 00:29 - +254 795 220161: *Coffee Farming Agribusiness: Key Determinants of Yield and Berry Quality.* 

When it comes to coffee farming, the factors that influence yields per tree and the quality of coffee berries are numerous. However, it's crucial to understand which factors have the most significant impact. Here's an in-depth look at what truly determines the performance of a coffee farm:
1. *Age of the Coffee Trees* 
The age of the coffee tree plays a pivotal role in both the quantity and quality of the harvest. Younger coffee trees (typically under 5 years) are more productive, producing more berries compared to older trees. This is similar to the analogy of young cows being more productive milkers. As trees age, their primary branches become less fruitful, and flowering occurs mostly at the edges of these branches, resulting in lower yields.
Rejuvenation: This process, which involves cutting back older trees to stimulate the growth of new, young stems, is essential for maintaining high productivity. *While it may seem counterintuitive and painful to cut back mature trees, rejuvenation leads to significantly higher yields in the long run, often starting to show results in two years.* This rejuvenation process is best done every 5-6 years by cutting a portion of the farm (1/3 or 1/4) to allow for the growth of younger, more productive stems.
2. *Pruning for Productivity* .
 Pruning is vital for increasing yields by enhancing the tree‚Äôs ability to flower. Flowering is a critical phase for coffee trees, and its success is determined by two factors: sufficient sunlight and water (rain). Proper pruning ensures that the coffee tree has a structure that allows sunlight to penetrate deeper into the branches and encourages robust flowering. *The better the pruning, the more flowers and, consequently, more berries the tree will produce.* 
Other factors include:
3. Nutrient Management and Soil Health
Healthy, well-nourished soil supports the growth of the coffee tree and improves its resistance to pests and diseases.
4. Pest and Disease Control
Maintaining good pest and disease management practices is critical for ensuring the health of the coffee trees. IPDM practices, including the use of biological control agents, organic pesticides, and regular monitoring, can help maintain a healthy coffee farm and prevent infestations.
5. Environmental Factors
Coffee trees thrive in specific climatic conditions, including consistent rainfall, moderate temperatures, and altitude. Any significant shifts in weather patterns, such as prolonged droughts or excessive rainfall, can negatively impact both the yields and the quality of the coffee.

In conclusion, *the highest determining factors for both coffee yields and berry quality are rejuvenation and pruning.* These practices ensure that coffee trees remain productive and capable of flowering properly. While soil health, pest and disease management, and climate are important, they are secondary to the structural maintenance of the trees. Understanding the life cycle of the coffee tree and the importance of rejuvenation can lead to sustainable, higher-quality yields, ultimately boosting a farmer's agribusiness.

Issued: 20, November 2024.

Denaza Agroconsultancy

24/11/2024, 23:49 - +254 795 220161: OVERCOMING THE DREADFUL EFFECTS OF COFFEE LEAF RUST (CLR) IN THE UPCOMING AND FUTURE SEASONS.

One of the most destructive diseases affecting coffee is Coffee Leaf Rust (CLR), caused by Hemileia vastatrix.This disease reduces coffee yield and quality, with climate change and poor management practices exacerbating its spread.The SL variety, in particular, has faced severe losses due to CLR. This article discusses methods to manage CLR and ensure a sustainable future for coffee farming.

CLR is a fungal disease that affects coffee plant leaves, reducing photosynthesis and leading to lower yields. It is characterized by orange spots on the upper leaf surface and yellow powder on the underside. The disease thrives in humid, moist conditions, spreading via water droplets. While SL and K7 varieties are highly susceptible, resistant varieties like Ruiru 11 and partially resistant Batian are more resilient.


The SL variety has been severely impacted by CLR. This disease leads to significant crop loss,forcing farmers to invest in costly fungicides and control measures.This year(2024) CLR has affected most farms with Sl in Kenya.

CLR can be managed through several practices:

1.Avoid Overhead Irrigation and Overspraying: Since CLR thrives in moist conditions, reducing moisture on the leaves is essential.

2. Proper Pruning for Air Circulation: moisture dry faster thus reducing the chance of infection.

3.Rejuvenation:By cutting back old,weak stems promotes healthy,disease-resistant growth.

4.Proper Nutrition: Fertilizing coffee plants with the right nutrients helps strengthen the plant's natural defenses against CLR.

5. Planting or Grafting with Resistant Varieties:The most effective long-term solution is planting resistant varieties like Ruiru 11 or grafting resistant varieties onto susceptible rootstocks.

6. Use of Curative and Preventive Chemicals: Fungicides like Klassic, rustblast  and Twiga Hypox can manage CLR if applied at the right time. Curative fungicides should be used when about 10% of the leaves show symptoms.Copper fungicides are preventive.


The impact of CLR on SL and other susceptible varieties is significant but manageable.By adopting good agricultural practices, such as proper irrigation, pruning, nutrition, and the use of fungicides, farmers can reduce the disease's impact. However, the most effective long-term solution is the adoption of resistant varieties like Ruiru 11 or the grafting of susceptible varieties.

Although transitioning to resistant varieties may involve upfront costs, the long-term benefits in terms of yield and disease management far outweigh the challenges Embracing these resilient practices is essential to ensuring the sustainability of coffee farming in a changing climate.

Issued: 24 November 2024

01/01/2025, 12:55 - +254 701 641933: Happy new year farmers in 2025 my message is Never Let the Soil Dry: A Key Principle in Regenerative Agriculture
Not only in coffee but
Soil is life. It is the foundation of all terrestrial ecosystems and the silent force behind the food we eat, the air we breathe, and the water we drink. Yet, too often, it is overlooked, abused, and left to deteriorate. One of the most critical, yet simple, principles in regenerative agriculture is this: Never let the soil dry.

The Science of Moisture and Soil Health

Healthy soil is more than dirt‚Äîit is a living ecosystem teeming with microorganisms, fungi, and organic matter that work in harmony to sustain plant life. Soil moisture is the lifeblood of this system, acting as a conduit for nutrients, enabling microbial activity, and maintaining soil structure. When soil dries out, this balance collapses:

Microbial death: Beneficial microorganisms die or go dormant without adequate moisture, disrupting nutrient cycling.

Soil compaction: Dry soil hardens and loses its porosity, making it difficult for roots to penetrate and reducing water infiltration when it does rain.

Erosion: Dry, exposed soil is vulnerable to wind and water erosion, stripping away the organic matter that took years to accumulate.

Regenerative Practices to Keep the Soil Moist

In regenerative agriculture, we seek to mimic natural systems, which rarely leave soil exposed or dry. Here are the key strategies to maintain soil moisture:

1. Mulching

A thick layer of mulch‚Äîmade from straw, leaves, wood chips, or crop residues‚Äîacts as a protective blanket over the soil. Mulch:

Reduces evaporation by shielding the soil from direct sunlight.

Prevents rain from compacting the soil surface.

Slowly decomposes, adding organic matter to the soil.

2. Cover Crops

Nature abhors bare soil. Cover crops such as legumes, grasses, or clover provide a living cover that keeps the soil cool and shaded, preventing moisture loss. Their roots:

Improve water infiltration.

Stabilize the soil structure.

Enhance the water-holding capacity of the soil.

3. Minimal Tillage

Tilling the soil disrupts its structure, breaks up fungal networks, and exposes moisture to evaporation. By minimizing tillage, we preserve the soil's natural water-retention capabilities and protect the microbial life that thrives in undisturbed soil.

4. Organic Matter

Soil rich in organic matter acts like a sponge, holding water during dry spells and releasing it slowly to plant roots. Composting and using animal manure are powerful ways to boost organic matter content.

5. Agroforestry and Shade Crops

Trees and shrubs planted alongside crops provide shade, reducing soil temperature and evaporation. Their deep roots also draw water from deeper layers of the soil, helping to stabilize moisture levels.

The Role of Soil Moisture in Climate Resilience

With unpredictable weather patterns and prolonged droughts becoming more frequent, keeping soil moist is no longer optional‚Äîit is essential for survival. Moist soils are better equipped to absorb heavy rains, reducing flooding, and to endure dry spells, ensuring crops survive and thrive.

Moreover, moist soil acts as a carbon sink, capturing carbon dioxide from the atmosphere and locking it into organic matter. This makes it a powerful ally in the fight against climate change.

A Call to Action

"Never let the soil dry" is not just a farming technique; it is a philosophy that acknowledges the interdependence of water, soil, and life. It calls us to steward the land with care, ensuring that future generations inherit soil that is rich, fertile, and alive.

If you are a small-scale farmer, a gardener, or simply a lover of the earth, let this principle guide you. Protect your soil. Cover it, nurture it, and never let it dry.

Together, we can regenerate the land and heal the planet‚Äîone drop of moisture at a time.

02/01/2025, 08:35 - +254 722 442781: Some information here isn't as accurate as presented .
1. Cover crops do not conserve moisture . Water in the soil is lost through 3 means .
(a) evaporation.  Through the soil surface. 
(b) uptake by plants through transpiration.    This contributes to the highest loss of moisture in the soil, and it is erroneous to assume that cover crops help in retaining moisture.  Cover crops compete for moisture with the main crop and are like weeds .
(c) infiltration below the root zone .

Shade trees /Agro forestry.  I would like farmers to assess for themselves and see whether there are differences in performance between shaded and unshaded crops. 
Shading reduces photosynthesis, and no crop can produce optimally under shade. A shaded  coffee tree may look healthy but will always produce less than the unshaded one.

02/01/2025, 12:13 - +254 735 819129: Critically and scientifically look at this statement "never let the soil dry". This man is very accurate. Cover crops conserve moisture. Allow me give you a simple illustration. Measure  2 small fields of 2m squared next to one another. Make sure that no shade is not next to them. Plant potato vines in one of them and leave the other unplanted. Expose both fields to equal weather conditions for a while. Test for moisture content of both fields and write back to this context. Similarly,carry out this experiment to shaded and unshaded soils. Secondly, water absorbed from the soil by the plant is used by the plant in a process called anabolism before transpiration. It doesn't run through like water in a pipeline <This message was edited>
02/01/2025, 12:39 - +254 722 442781: It is not a trial that I am going to do , I have done it on several occasions.  But logic thinking alone will inform you the following. 
1. Bare land without  a cover crop may lose water in only two ways .
(a) evaporation.  Which is the loss of water at the surface of the soil . Once the water evaporates at the surface,  the water molecules below the surface move up through capillary action and then evaporate .
2. Water infiltrating below the root zone .

Alternatively, on a ground that has crops , the loss is on 3 ways . The two mentioned above and through transpiration and finally evaporation at the leaf surface. 
Water lost by plants by the process of evapotranspiration is much more than evaporation because it is taken below the surface. A plant behaves like a pipe inserted on the ground and the difference is that water emitted at the surface is inform of tiny microscopic droplets. 

A ha  of cabbages may emit to the atmosphere 60 cubic meter of water and remain dry in the 3rd day while a similar Ha with 1 week cabbage crop may go for a week plus before requiring more water .

Any cover crop with leaves covering the ground acts like small tubelets tapping water from the soil .

02/01/2025, 13:53 - +254 722 442781: üòä what is evaporating, my friend? Water, not the soil .
Let me give you a practical example.  

1 ha of coffee seedlings on a normal day may get an irrigation of 1.5mm in 5 days ,while a full-grown coffee will take 5mm .
Why ? 
The bigger the leaf surface area and deeper root system, the higher the water uptake . 

If you apply 5mm of water on two surfaces measuring 10m¬≤ ,one  mulched and the other one  un mulched and exposed them to sunshine  for a period of time , the unmulched ground will lose more water .  
The reason is that the mulch material will keep the ground cooler and, therefore, less evaporation..

If the two fields are left bare , they will lose water at the same rate .

If you ask someone to turn the soil in one  field , it will lose more water than the un disturbed field .

If you plant potatoes as you had suggested earlier ,  the planted field will lose more water than the bare field . And the bigger the potatoes cover on the ground or rather the bigger the potatoes, leaf surface area, the higher the loss . 

If you take time to study irrigation, hii conversion itaisha but am not surprised because it took me time to understand the concept.

02/01/2025, 14:40 - +254 722 442781: If this was not a farmers group where correct information matters  , I would have left this matter to rest . But in this case , good understanding is key .
 When the idea about moisture conservation was posted , I read it , understood it, and I responded with what I didn't agree with.  

I fully understood the message, and I disputed that cover crops can conserve moisture because they can not. 

How is moisture lost in the soil as far as crop production is concerned? 

Through evaporation on the soil surface and through evaporation at the leaf surface.. the bigger the leaf cover on the surface, the higher the loss . 

Evaporation from the soil is a process where the top layer, eg 1st one inch  of the soil, loses water to the atmosphere,  water from the second layer 2"  moves up to replace the lost water through capillarity . Tuko pamoja mpaka hapo .

Under normal circumstances,  or on bare soil , water movement upwards only happens through capillarity .. Right ? 

On a cropped surface,  water movement upwards happens through 2 methods , via plant roots after absorption and capillarity.   So, cropped surface loses water via two processes.  

Whereas a cropped surface may appear shaded , the water lost through plant leaves is higher than that t of bare ground because the loss is through capillarity and root absorption from as deep as the depth of the plant roots .

Let me take you to irrigation..
 
1 ha of potatoes that is two weeks old will require 20 cubic meters of irrigation per day, while the same  when 10 weeks old  and fully covered, the ground will require 50 m cubic of water per day

Why ? 
It is because of the difference in the leaf  surface area . The higher the leaf surface, the higher the loss of water .

Any growing plant ,whether grass , weeds ,target crop, or cover crop, needs water for it to grow, and therefore, every growing crop contributes to loss of moisture in the soil ..

In order to conserve moisture in soil , use dead materials as mulch.

02/01/2025, 18:32 - +254 722 442781: @254722593749 and all the agronomists in the house .
Let's discuss rain drop retention and I will start by sharing my thoughts. 

This is my theory .
Any drop of water that infiltrate into the soil below the root zone must come up not unless it goes too deep .

If the ground is compacted , the top few inches of the soil get saturated and therefore results to run off which is a big loss .
My thinking is that we should retain the rain water within the cropping area . 
How ? 
By creating water basins around coffee trees. 

A basin of 2m by 2m by 0.15m high will hold 600 litres of water which would run off if no basin is moulded .
600 litres x 550 trees of SL in an acre = 330,000 litres of water that can be allowed to inflitrate into the soil .

06/01/2025, 14:49 - +254 722 593749: I like how healthy discussions on coffee matters take place in this forum. One thing that's coming out clear is that what works best for one farmer may not automatically work for another. Our experiences are quite as diverse as our farms and conditions which are different even when comparing 2 farms adjacent to each other.
C.A.N application is a controversial issue and not quite clear. It's assimilation and uptake as a straight inorganic fertiliser that only supplies Nitrogen makes leaf surface to develop softness and succulence making which is a predisposing condition for proliferation of CLR.
Farmers who've substituted it's use with compound N.P.K have noted a significant drop in the incidences of CBD & CLR.
However as I'll always advise successful coffee farming is a combination of several factors and agronomy practices in the coffee farm.

By Agronomist Dennis,Mkulima kahawa mkononi.

PLANTING COFFEE -1
Land preparation and spacing.* 

[Thank you for reading this free newsletter. *Share*, distribute, and republish freely with credit to the source as 'Agronomist Dennis.'
For a personalized Coffee calendar and more details; For professional assistance on the WHAT, WHEN, WHERE and HOW on Coffee and the coffee value-chain in Kenya; For more free resources including tips on growing, production, and marketing, contact: *Agronomist Dennis, a Kenyan-Based Agronomist who may be contacted on (+254) 0795220161.* Agronomist Dennis Is A Champion For Farmers and Farming Communities in Kenya.]

PLANTING COFFEE - 1.
 *Land preparation and spacing.* 
Planting is the foundation of every crop such as perennials, annuals and also biennials.It refers to the process of putting seeds or young plants(seedlings) in the ground to grow.
In coffee,planting involves placing prenurtured seedlings to the ground and its the second stage of coffee production after nursery management.

Reasons for planting coffee.
1.To increase land acreage with coffee.
2.Fill gaps in coffee field
3.To start new coffee farm in a land that was initially for other purpose.
4.Replace old varieties with disease resistant varieties such as Batian and Ruiru 11.

Coffee growing land should:
‚Ä¢Be a land owned by the farmer since coffee is a long-term crop.
‚Ä¢Be well drained.Thus avoid waterlogged land.
‚Ä¢Fallow land or that which is due to be fallow after harvest of food crop.

Land to avoid when planting coffee:
-Land that is used for main food crops production.
-Land that is forested. Coffee planted in Land that was initially a forest will have high incidences of Armillaria and MUST be avoided.

 *Land preparation to plant coffee.* 
This should be done in the month of January to February.Land preparation involves:
‚Ä¢Digging out perennial weeds while the annual ones can be slashed so as not to leave the soil bare
‚Ä¢Prepare terraces and plant stabilising grasses along the contour if on a steep slope before planting.
‚Ä¢Plant bananas or shade trees.
‚Ä¢Mark where the holes should be in a straight line,considering the spacing.( *For this service consult -0795220161)* 

 *Spacing in coffee.* 
The spacing to be used is determined by the variety one chooses to plant.Planting coffee in correct spacing means there will be no competition for light,nutrients and water.From observation the spacing should be:
Ruiru 11 -7ft√ó7ft.
Batian     -9ft√ó9ft
Sl &K7      -9ft√ó9ft.

Issued:January 19, 2025

General Notice: This material is for general information to a large audience. Thus, results vary. Always contact a professional for support based on your specific needs, requirements, and situation.

19/01/2025, 22:24 - +254 722 593749: Propagation. Ruiru 11 plantlets are developed from sowing pure seeds on nursery to germinate and develop in ready for transplanting in the field. Grafted Ruiru 11 plantlets are developed from a union between root stock(SL 28 or 34) and Scion (the top part of the plantlets which is either from a pure stand of Ruiru 11 or a clonal garden. Once the union heals the plantlets are ready for transplanting.

20/01/2025, 14:28 - +254 722 442781: A tree with a large canopy is also expected to have  big and deep roots than that with a smaller canopy.  It is a fact that SL varieties have bigger canopies and, therefore, deeper root systems.  
If SL is allowed to establish to over 8 years and then budded with Ruiru 11, automatically Ruiru will benefit from the deeper root system attained as a result of carrying a bigger canopy.

If a young rootstock of SL is grafted with a  Ruiru scion  , logically, it will not develop a deeper root system as it would normally happen when carrying a larger canopy. 
This is my theory, and I am sure grafting SL with Ruiru scion is also a theory.
20/01/2025, 14:37 - +254 722 442781: roots are difficult to study under field conditions, canopy temperature has been applied as an indirect way of assessing the root depth as higher water uptake and leaf transpiration is related to a cooler canopy. Canopy stay-green characters

Peekgrow Organic foliar:

It's an organic foliar customised for coffee plant (has all nutrients required by the coffee plant).
It has also been tested and proven for other crops such as fruit trees and horticultural crops.

Benefits of using Peek Organic foliar.
1.Its organic thus safe for using in most crops-coffee, maize,tomato,avocado, Napier etc.
2.Its cost effective - has Spreader and Sticker in it,thus cuts the cost of buying them separately.
3.Has high  NPK,zinc and boron and other micro-nutrients.

Thus peekgrow foliar is sustainable (it's economical, environmentally friendly and socially just).

Interval for spray:
Spray after every fortnight(14days) if deficiency is prolonged and after  every month if no deficiency.

Rate of spray:
50ml/20L in coffee and fruit orchards 
30ml/20L in horticultural crops.

Price:
250ml. -300 KSh.
500ml. -550 Ksh
1L.       -1000Ksh
5L.       -4800 Ksh
10L.     -9700 Ksh
20L.    -19500 Ksh.


Make your order.

05/02/2025, 12:00 - +254 795 220161: *MAJOR BEST AGRONOMIC PRACTICES(BAPs) IN COFFEE FOR FEBRUARY 2025.* 
(By Agronomist Dennis wa Mkulima kahawa mkononi)
 _Hole digging and shade tree establishment for new farm._

One month for 2025 is gone.Three important questions a farmer will need to ask themselves.What is my goal and target in yields for my coffee farm?What did i do in January that will help me achieve my goal?Am i still enthusiastic to follow guidance and seek advice from a professional agronomist to help achieve my target?
My hope its that these questions will help guide you all through.

Remember:The long days agriculture is far much gone;nowadays we are in an era of kilimo Biashara (Agriculture for money/profits).If its not this,a good advice ,abandon it.

The major Best Agronomic Practices for coffee this February 2025 includes:
1.Prunning and rejuvenation.
Its disappointing walking to some farms to find out that some farmers are yet to prune.Prunning is a requirement that need not to be ignored.Its what the coffee requires to flower well, flowering will inturn determine the yields.On the other hand, Rejuvenation or the changing of cycle will help get yields for a  long period.Do these before flowering.

2.Weeding and Mulching 
Weeds compete with the coffee plant for water and nutrients.Ensure under the canopy its weedfree and mulched.Slash between rows.

3.Fertilization and Liming.
Its important applying lime in your farm, either dolomitic or calcium lime as per the recommendation of a soil test.
Apply a general foliar,wuxual,omex,biofol,calcibor,zinc and boron.You can as well use Peekgrow(an organic foliar customised for coffee).If the berries are still expanding and the early crop much,ensure you do the foliar sprays with high NPK .

4.Hole digging and shade tree planting.
I believe some of us want to extend our coffee farms, some are beginning to farm coffee and infilling.
Ensure you dig a good hole by end of this month.Even though a 2ft x 2ft is the recommended hole,a 3ft x 3ft has,from experience,done well .Lets Discuss this in the next article this month.
Its important if you are a start up or intend to extend your farm to plant shade trees after you are done with hole digging.

 *NOTE :* 
‚Ä¢ *Composting* - Its important you continue making compost for applying on your trees come April.
 *‚Ä¢Record Keeping* -Its agribusiness we are in,thus recording keeping is key to trace farm activities and the cost.
 *‚Ä¢Soil testing* -Ensure you do a soil test to know the nutrient need for your farm.

We offer these services to farmers:
Training your workers
Farm visits
Soik tests.
Record keeping 

Issued On: 5th January 2025.

11/02/2025, 17:43 - +254 795 220161: üåé *Attention to all coffee Farmers!* 

*COFFEE PLANTING 2:* 

*THE PROCESS OF HOLE DIGGING FOR PLANTING COFFEE & AVOCADO.* 

 _The best hole for planting coffee and Avocado._

What are the me best measurements?
Relating a 2ft √ó2ft by a 3ft x 3ft hole.
Why dig a hole.
How(Steps) to dig a hole for coffee planting.

In construction works,the foundation laid relates to the type of house being constructed.The taller the building,the stronger the foundation will be.
The foundation in coffee agribusiness is how we plant.Thus, planting is very crucial and key and should be thorough and done professionally.

Coffee seedlings are planted in holes when there are rains or the soil has enough moisture.Holes should be dug 2 months before actual planting.

We dig holes in coffee to:
1.Break the hardpans in soil to allow for easier root penetration.
2.Allows for easier penetration of water and air during seeding growth.

 *What is the best size for a coffee hole?*

Even though a 2ft x 2ft hole is the recommended and works well,a 3ft x 3ft hole(from a number of farmers experience) has proven to give much better results. This is because of the ease and faster  root elongation due to deep loose soil which also facilitates trunk and branches elongation.
We will discuss more during backfilling and actual planting.

 *Steps to digging a good quality hole:* 

Hoping you as a farmer has already done land preparation in January,you will now follow the following steps:
1. Mark your farm and space the the marks depending with the Variety.Use pegs to mark.
2. Dig the hole 3ft x3ft x3ft using a fork Jembe.The top soil(1.5ft) should be put separate from the Subsoil .Ensure the peg is at the centre as you dig the hole.
3. Mark the top soil using a peg .Do this for each hole.You will require this to mix with manure during backfilling.
4. Leave the hole open for about A month . It's left open so that it can gets cracks which will make water infiltration efficient and facilitate good root development.

 *NOTE:* 
1. *Soil testing* is very key at this stage of hole digging if you didn't do it in January.Ensure you test your soil.
2. Also plant shade trees in the coffee farms at this stage . Plant such trees as albizia,crotin,Markhamia,Cordia or even a food crop as Banana's.
3. Make terraces before hole digging if its on a sloping land.
4. Don't spray at your coffee when there are flowers. Let them fall first.
5. For the coffee with a crop, spray zinc and boron foliars and alsohigh NPK foliars .

For more information on Coffee and avocado agribusiness, contact us through:
0795220161/0751221613.

Issued on: 11th February 2025.

By: Agronomist Dennis 
Lead Agronomist at Denaza Agroconsulting ltd.

13/02/2025, 13:23 - +254 795 220161: Attention Coffee Farmers:

 *RAW COFFEE BEANS FOR EXPORT.* 

*Key Requirements for Export from Kenya to the World*

 *Why Export Coffee?* 
Exporting coffee provides a valuable opportunity for Kenyan farmers to access international markets and earn better prices for their high-quality beans. By meeting global demand, Kenya‚Äôs coffee farmers can expand their reach and establish long-term relationships with buyers.

 *Sources for Raw Coffee Beans for Export:* 

A) *National Coffee Exchange (NCE)* ‚Äì Coffee can be sourced through the NCE via the auction system by participating in bidding.
B) *Direct Sales* ‚Äì Coffee can also be sold directly to international buyers, but this requires specific agreements and approval from the Coffee Directorate.

 *Exporter Requirements: Rules and Regulations* 
To become a licensed coffee exporter in Kenya, the following key requirements must be met:

1. *Export License* 
Issued by the Coffee Directorate under the Agriculture and Food Authority (AFA). This confirms that the exporter complies with the Coffee Act regulations.

2. *Certificate of Origin* 
Issued by the Kenya National Chamber of Commerce and Industry (KNCCI). This document verifies that the coffee being exported is grown and produced in Kenya.

3. *Phytosanitary Certificate* 
Issued by the Kenya Plant Health Inspectorate Service (KEPHIS). This certificate ensures that the coffee is free from pests and diseases, and meets international phytosanitary standards.

 *Key Procedures for Coffee Export* 

1. Registration with the Coffee Board (now under AFA) ‚Äì All exporters must register with the relevant authority.
2. Obtaining an Export License ‚Äì A valid export license is mandatory for all exporters.
3. Quality Standards ‚Äì Exporters must ensure the coffee meets the required quality standards for grading and classification.
4. Obtaining Phytosanitary Certificates ‚Äì Ensure the coffee meets health and safety requirements by obtaining this certificate.
5. Obtaining a Certificate of Origin ‚Äì Confirm that the coffee is produced in Kenya.
6. Coffee Sample Submission ‚Äì Buyers may request coffee samples for quality analysis and grading.
7. Compliance with Export Regulations ‚Äì All export procedures, including customs declarations and documentation, must be followed in accordance with Kenyan export regulations.

References:
Kenya Coffee Board
Coffee Act Regulations

Issued on: 13th February 2025

14/02/2025, 07:50 - +254 795 220161: *Phosphorus Deficiency in Coffee:* 

Phosphorus is a major nutrient,its required in high quantities by the plants.

 *Importance of Phosphorus.* 
‚Ä¢ Phosphorus is essential for root development and energy transfer within the plant. 
‚Ä¢  It's essential for flower development and fruit set.

 *Causes of Phosphorus Deficiency* 

1. In tropical soils, phosphates can form with *low solubilities* , making phosphorus immobile
2. *High demand for phosphorus* can coincide with *dry soil conditions.* This explains why during the dry months,its deficiency is evident .

 *Deficiency Diagnosis.*
The Symptoms includes:-
1. *Older leaves* develop irregular *yellow* areas that may spread to the whole leaf.
2. Leaves may turn red or violet under severe conditions.
3. Leaves may develop a purple or bronze tint.
4. Leaves may be smaller than normal
5. Flowering and fruit set may be delayed or reduced.

 *Correction*
1. Use organic manures.
2. Apply high Phosphorus foliars.
3. Apply single superphosphate to treat deficiency symptoms.

18/02/2025, 19:22 - +254 701 641933: White Stem Borer

Symptoms and damage

Wood shavings extruded by larvae burrowing in the stem
Ring-barking at the base of the trunk
Oblong holes visible on the trunks left by larvae after entering the trunk
Visible round holes on trunks left by emerging adults
Yellowing of foliage and eventual death of trees


Management

Mechanical control

Kill the larva(e) that is already in the stem by inserting a wire/spoke into the tunnel
Physically collect and kill the beetle at the onset of rains
Chemical control

Paint or spray a 90 cm band above the ground on the coffee trunk with a recommended insecticide. Repeat after one year and every second year.
Insert a cotton ball soaked in an insecticide through the tunnel in incidences where the larva has entered into the stem.

*Coffee leaf rust.*
 _Hemileia vastatrix_

‚Ä¢This is a disease affecting the Sl and K7 variety.
‚Ä¢Its Spread mostly by raindrops and is prevalent in hot climates.
‚Ä¢Can also be spread by wind,animals and even humans as they pass through the farm

 *Economic importance:*
‚Ä¢Leads to leaf fall reducing 'food factory'  this the whole coffee tree can dry up 
‚Ä¢Can reduce to crop fail.

 *IPDM Strategy.*
‚Ä¢Good prunning and rejuvenation.
‚Ä¢Proper feeding (nutrition)
‚Ä¢Reducing stress by weeding and shading.
‚Ä¢ *Planting resistant variety* as Ruiru 11 and Batian.
‚Ä¢Preventive copper fungicides.
‚Ä¢Curative fungicides as ,Classic,twiga hypox and tabibu.Always alternate these for effective control.
‚Ä¢Control  when  10%(1 out of 10) leaves is affected.

Denaza Agroconsulting.
Farmers oriented.

21/02/2025, 07:34 - +254 795 220161: *Mealybugs and Scales* 

These pests are found on the growing area of the coffee plant where they suck the sweet sap from the plant and may lead to drying up of the plant.

‚Ä¢Also blackening of the leaves that hinder photosynthesis processes in the plant due to formation of mould due to the sugary excrete.

 *The association between Mealybugs,scales and black ant (Thigiriri)*
‚Ä¢This answers the question why leaves blackens.
‚Ä¢The scales and mealybugs suck sugary sap and excretes.
‚Ä¢The black ants feeds on the sugary excrete thus removes the waste from the plant.
‚Ä¢The excrete would otherwise eliminate the scales and mealybugs naturally.
‚Ä¢As these three moves they leave marks of the sugary excrete on leaf surfaces and berries.
‚Ä¢Mould that is in the air grows on the leaves thus they blacken.

 *Management of the pests.*
‚Ä¢During Scouting,the presence of black ants moving up and down the coffee tree justifies presence of the scakes and mealybugs.
‚Ä¢Spray a tank mix of Segatron (50ml) OR D-ctron oil(100ml) and teepol(50ml) in a 20l pump.
‚Ä¢Spot spray(Selective)only the affected trees in the farm.
‚Ä¢Prune branches touching the ground.

22/02/2025, 13:58 - +254 795 220161: TO DO BEFORE END OF
FEBRUARY 2025 IN THE COFFEE FARMS.:

Its important that by the end of this month that every farmer should have :
1. Dug planting holes(3ft x 3ft).
2. Done soil testing 
3. Lime application -To lower acidity and raise pH.
4. Weeded and mulched the coffee farms.
5. Sprayed a general foliar as Biofol,wuxual,omex, Peekgrow and Zinc and Boron foliars.
6. Spray preventive fungicide as green copper and if leaf rust is evident spray curative fungicides .This is for those with the Susceptible varieties as Sl and K7 .

Advantages of proper  spacing in coffee. 
Proper coffee plant spacing is crucial because it directly impacts the coffee yield by allowing adequate sunlight, air circulation, and root development for each plant, leading to healthier growth and higher quality coffee bean.

Spacing:
1. Ruiru 11 -CRI recommends 6ft x6 ft but  a 7ft x 8ft has worked well .
2. Batian 8ft x 9ft has also worked well.(The recommendations for CRI 7 ft by 8ft)
3. Sl and K7 varieties,: 9ft by 9ft.

NB// The system a farmer chooses to use whether single -stem or multiple stems also determines the spacing.

THE VALUE OF SECONDARY BRANCHES IN COFFEE.
A secondary branch is that branch originating from a primary branch  in a coffee plant.
Secondary branches¬†should be:
‚Ä¢ 6 inches from the stem, 
‚Ä¢ 2 knots apart, 
‚Ä¢  On alternating sides.
‚Ä¢ Should only be on the part of the primary branch that has been harvested 
‚Ä¢Secondary branches should be left out during prunning.

As the primary branch age, mostly especially on all other variety apart from Ruiru grafted,the productivity goes towards the tip of the branch.This necessities the need for secondary branches.
Thus,the secondary branches help increase yields in terms of quantity.

‚Ä¢Leave only *4-6 secondary branches* on one primary Branch.

By Agronomist Dennis.
Lead Agronomist @Denaza Agroconsulting ltd

24/02/2025, 12:23 - +254 701 641933: CoffeeBerry Disease (Colletotrichum kahawae)

Symptoms

On flowers: Dark brown blotches/streaks on the petals.  Flowers may be destroyed but loses from flower infection are generally not serious
On green berries: Small dark sunken patches/lesions which spread rapidly and may cover the whole berry. Infected berries may be shed or remain on the trees in a black shriveled condition  
On ripe berries: Dark sunken lesions with black dots spreading rapidly on the ripe berries (late Blight)
On leaves: Brown marginal spots. However, leaf infection is not common 
Severe infections may cause the die-back of twigs and branches
24/02/2025, 12:24 - +254 701 641933: Conditions favoring high disease incidences

Cool temperatures ‚Äì 18-200 C
High humidity - encourages spores production
Rainfall ‚Äì rain droplets disperse the spores to the rest of the tree. After the dispersal, at least 5 hours of wetness on the berries are required for the spores to germinate. Rainfall occurring in the late afternoon is therefore likely to provide suitable conditions for infection

24/02/2025, 21:24 - +254 701 641933: Key benefits of using solar dryers for coffee in Kenya:
Quality Improvement:
Solar dryers provide a controlled drying environment, ensuring even drying of coffee cherries, preventing uneven heating and preserving the coffee bean's flavor profile and aroma. 
Faster Drying Time:
Compared to traditional sun drying, solar dryers significantly reduce drying time, allowing farmers to process more coffee in a shorter period. 
Weather Protection:
The enclosed design protects coffee beans from rain and dust contamination, which can significantly impact quality, especially during unpredictable weather conditions. 
Labor Efficiency:
Solar dryers require less manual labor as they automatically regulate the drying process, reducing the need for constant turning and monitoring. 
Cost-Effectiveness:
By minimizing drying time and improving quality, solar dryers can lead to higher market prices for coffee, offsetting the initial investment cost. 
Environmental Sustainability:
Solar dryers utilize renewable solar energy, contributing to a reduced carbon footprint compared to fossil fuel-based drying methods.

26/02/2025, 17:26 - +254 795 220161: *Effective Scouting and Monitoring for Pest and deficiency Control in Sustainable Farming."* 

‚Ä¢Crop scouting is the practice of observing crops to identify potential issues like pests, diseases, and nutrient deficiencies.
‚Ä¢ It's a key part of crop management that can help growers make informed decisions and optimize yields. 

 *Why scout.?* 
‚Ä¢ Helps identify problems early so they don't cause significant damage 
‚Ä¢Helps growers take proactive measures to improve crop health and yield.
‚Ä¢Helps growers monitor the spread of pests and diseases.
‚Ä¢Helps growers detect nutritional requirements.

Scouting process.
First its good sampling a number of crops to scout from.In coffee its advisable to scot atleast 5 per 200stems,in Avocado scout 10 out of 100 trees.
After samplin scout by:-
1. By closely inspecting plants for signs of stress, pests, and diseases 
2. By using insect traps, such as sticky traps and pheromones 
3. By randomly inspecting plants throughout the production area 
4. By gathering and recording information about a particular crop on a regular basis.

 *Note:* 
‚Ä¢In a serious farmer will scout their coffee/avocado farm atleast twice a week.
‚Ä¢Scout often if you identify a pest or you are controlling it.
‚Ä¢Don't scout those in the neighborhood but you can place traps to know direction of pests.
‚Ä¢Understand deficiencies to be able to note them.

By Agronomist Dennis.(0795220161)
Lead Agronomist @Denaza Agroconsulting ltd.

For enquiries on coffee,avocado and dairy farming.Use WhatsApp number above.

27/02/2025, 22:17 - +254 795 220161: *A REPORT FROM A FARM VISIT CONDUCTED IN MRS.KIDUNA'S FARM IN KAMUCEGE,KAMBU ON 27/02/2025.*

CROPS:
COFFEE & BANANA'S.
Coffee- 2700 stems.
 Bananas -120.

This report is as a result of history taken and observations made during scouting on the day of visit .

 *Results and observations:* 
-Banana's are doing well apart from a few that have dried up due to wilt and some moles.
-Some stumps have many suckers emerging.
 *Coffee:*
-Lime application done on mulch.
-Manure had been applied in sime part of the farm despite the high temperatures.
-Rejuvenation has been done and the farm has young stems.
-Prunning has been done correctly.
-Shade levels very low or none at all 
-The small seedlings are drying up due to sun's intensity.
-2024 yields was at 5300kg for the 2700stems in the farm.Gives an average of 1.96kgs/tree.
-Weeding well done.Herbicides used in some parts.
-Mulching has been done.
-No major pests and diseases.
-Mbuni's are still on the trees.
-Copper sprays to the grafted Ruiru .

 *Recommendations*:
Target 2025 - 13500kg (5kg/tree).
What to do?
1. Always apply half debe of fully composted manure in the long rains and short rains. Twice a year.
       You can as well alternate with        organic fertilizer.
2. Apply 160g/tree of NPK fertilizer 22.6.12 +S in the months of April and October, 2weeks after the rains.
3. Lime application.Apply 500g of agricultural lime per tree as demonstrated having removed the mulch.All land should be covered with lime in time of application.
4. Bananas: Apply NPK and manure with the rains.
-Also , for those that have dried,replace them with new suckers and apply lime before planting.
-Prune the suckers to have 4-5stems per stump.Also prune the banana leaves.
5. *Foliar sprays:* 
For Ruiru,its a heavy feeder.Thus,using foliars really helps to keep the crop.Thus spray foliars of zinc and boron and high NPK foliars as wuxual,biofol or omex, peekgrow every month.
-Spray also adaptive copper as feeds during the dry months or if green copper (70g).
-Also in the next 2 sprays,use calcibor.

6. Spray pesticides after scouting and identifying a pest
7. *Don't* use  herbicides to kill weeds 
8. *Biodiversity* Plant avocadoes(Hass ) on the hedges of the coffee farm and at the centre on the onset of raains.
9. Irrigation 
 With the high effect of climate change.Its good irrigating the coffee farm.and Mulching.

See the below photos for the farm.Thanks .

Report By Agronomist Dennis.

The Lead Agronomist @Denaza Agroconsulting ltd .

 *MAJOR BEST AGRONOMIC PRACTICES(BAPs) FOR MARCH _2025* 
(By Agronomist Dennis Wa Mkulima Kahawa Mkononi_ ).

The main challenge with most coffee farmers in the World is the ignorance of proper timing (the 'WHEN ") for the important agronomic practices. 

Correct timing for the Best Agronomic Practices(BAPs) in coffee farming is key to the final results of coffee production.
Here are the major practices to do in your coffee farms: 

1. *Backfilling of planting holes.* 
  How:-Organic materials chopped first(not a necessity,you can just mix soil).
In March we will know whyto backfill.
-Top soil mixed with manure
-Fill with subsoil mixed with manure untill the hole is heaped.
-Before the whole hole is covered,place a peg in the middle of the hole.

2. *Seedling acquisition and booking.-* Bring them near the farm where there is water and in an open field.
     ‚Ä¢Ensure you get certified seedlings.

3. Composting for use in coffee farms.Use organic wastes.

4. Weeding and mulching -weeds reduce yields by half through competing for nutrients with the coffee plant.
      ‚Ä¢Mulching helps prevent weed growth when it rains.

5. Acquisition of Fertilizer,DAP for planting , NPK fertilizer  for tue crop and manure/organic fertilizer.) 
‚Ä¢For organic fertilizer reach out to me.
‚Ä¢ *The fertilizer type is dependent on the results of a soil test.* 

6. *Foliar sprays* 
High NPK foliars are important for the bearing crop and zinc and Boron.
Akso spray captain P.

7. *Soil erosion control methods*  -terraces,gabions,mulch.
   ‚Ä¢ Its important controlling and preventing soil erosion with the coming rains.

02/03/2025, 18:15 - +254 721 552757: This is bacterial blight of coffee (BBC) caused by Pseudomonas syringae pv. Garcae.
It used to be confined to a few coffee growing areas in Kenya (Solai in Nakuru District and around Mt. Elgon). Recently a few cases have been reported in the East of Rift Valley.
02/03/2025, 18:16 - +254 722 240407: null
02/03/2025, 18:17 - +254 721 552757: The disease is favoured by cool wet weather. Lesions appear on leaves with water soaked margins at the start of infection. Leaves eventually dry up and roll inwards turning brown. Dead and dried leaves do not shed but remain attached to the plant. Symptoms occur on secondary or tertiary branches and in severe cases the heads may be affected. On twigs the terminal bud is attacked. Infection then extends downwards, resulting in dieback. Flowers and pin-heads shrivel and turn black.

The initial symptom is the blackening of a node often accompanied by blackening of the petiole and basal part of the leaf. This leads to death of the branch above the node and leaves on the branch turn brown and eventually necrotic (burnt). Severely affected trees appear scorched as if by fire. The bacterium persists on leaves, berries and on green and mature bark. During cool, wet weather, the bacterium multiplies and initiates an epidemic. The entire crop may be lost.
02/03/2025, 18:23 - +254 721 552757: How to control:
1. Desucker or cut off infected twigs (at least 5 cm from the point of infection) and collect them for burning.
2. Observe field hygiene by disinfecting tools used for pruning infected trees with a suitable disinfectant such as spirits with 70% alcohol. Implements used must be sterilised after making each cut to avoid the risk of infecting the cut surfaces of the twig with a carry-over inoculum.
3. Though not a fungal disease, use of copper sprays especially during wet seasons helps in controlling it. Spray at 2 week interval during the rains and 3 week interval after the rains. If you are in the hotspots, you can adopt spraying with copper just before, during and after flowering especially when this coincides with cool wet weather.
4. It is advisable to plant shade trees and wind breaks on exposed sides of BBC areas.
5. Avoid planting materials (seeds and seedlings) from known BBC areas.

Revolutionizing Coffee Farming: How AGRI-BIOTECH FARM INTERNATIONAL Solves Low Yields and Poor Quality

At AGRI-BIOTECH FARM INTERNATIONAL, we‚Äôve seen firsthand how farmers struggle with low coffee yields and inconsistent cherry quality. Many plantations suffer due to imbalanced soil pH, poor nutrient absorption, and improper tree management, leading to underdeveloped cherries and weak production cycles. But through precision agronomic practices, we‚Äôve turned these challenges into opportunities for higher yields and better coffee quality.

The Challenge: Low Yields and Poor Cherry Development

Many coffee farmers assume that a tree loaded with cherries guarantees a high yield. However, the real secret lies in the leaf-to-fruit ratio and the weight of each individual cherry. Trees with excessive fruit and insufficient leaf support suffer from nutrient competition, leading to:
‚úîÔ∏è Small, lightweight cherries.
‚úîÔ∏è Increased number of cherries per kilogram (up to 1,000 cherries per kg in poorly managed farms).
‚úîÔ∏è Low cup quality due to insufficient sugar and nutrient concentration.

Additionally, soil pH imbalance plays a major role in nutrient absorption. Coffee trees thrive best in a pH range of 5.5 to 6.5. Outside this range:

Too acidic (below 5.5): Nutrients like phosphorus, calcium, and magnesium become unavailable, leading to weak trees.

Too alkaline (above 6.5): Iron and zinc deficiencies emerge, affecting leaf health and overall growth.

With improper soil nutrition, even trees with potential for 10-20 kg per season end up producing only 2-5 kg, causing major financial losses for farmers.

Our Solution: Precision Agronomic Management for Maximum Yield

At AGRI-BIOTECH FARM INTERNATIONAL, we‚Äôve developed a tailored approach to coffee farming, focusing on:

1Ô∏è‚É£ Balanced Soil Nutrition & pH Regulation
‚úîÔ∏è We conduct soil testing to determine pH and nutrient deficiencies.
‚úîÔ∏è We apply agricultural lime where soil is too acidic, ensuring optimal nutrient absorption.
‚úîÔ∏è We use organic basal and foliar fertilizers to boost tree health and productivity.

2Ô∏è‚É£ Selective Pruning & Leaf-to-Fruit Ratio Optimization
‚úîÔ∏è We assess the physiological structure of each tree, balancing the number of cherries per branch.
‚úîÔ∏è We prune selectively, ensuring an ideal leaf-to-fruit ratio for maximum cherry weight and sugar concentration.
‚úîÔ∏è Well-pruned, healthy trees can produce 300-400 cherries per kg, compared to poorly managed trees that need 1,000 cherries per kg.

3Ô∏è‚É£ Targeted Feeding & Crop Care for Bigger, Heavier Cherries
‚úîÔ∏è Our nutrition strategy ensures that each berry develops proper weight and density, increasing overall coffee quality.
‚úîÔ∏è Farmers under our program achieve 10-20 kg per tree by aligning nutrients with physiological growth stages.
‚úîÔ∏è We focus on crop protection by reducing pest and disease pressure, ensuring cherries develop fully.

Proven Results: From Low Yields to Premium Coffee Production

Through our scientific approach, farmers experience:
‚úÖ Higher yields per tree (10-20 kg compared to 2-5 kg before intervention).
‚úÖ Increased P1 and P2 grading at the wet mill, meaning denser, high-quality coffee.
‚úÖ Healthier trees with longer productive lifespans.
‚úÖ Sustainable farming that maximizes soil health for long-term coffee success.

Your Farm Can Achieve the Same Results!
If you want higher yields, heavier cherries, and premium coffee grades, AGRI-BIOTECH FARM INTERNATIONAL is here to help.

19/03/2025, 22:01 - +254 795 220161: *Best agronomic practices in coffee .you should be following up with the onset of rains:* 
( _By Agronomist Dennis wa Mkulima kahawa Mkononi_ )

1. Seedlings delivery.
I believe you had booked  seedlings for planting in your farm.Its the high time you pick them from the certified nursery you had booked from.Let them be under direct sunlight in one week time to avoid sun scorching while in the
 field.

2.Fertilizer and manure delivery.
The rains are with us, and this will be our nutrition month to our coffee and other fruit trees.
Deliver these near the farms.
Ensure you purchase the fertilizer as per the results of a,soil test.
Most soils are deficient of organic matter,if you lack manure,you can use an organic fertilizer such as *Blackgold organic fertilizer* (contact us).

3.Weeding and mulching. 
Weeds compete with plants for moisture and nutrients.In coffee,weeds reduce the yields by half.
Mulching at this time is essential after weeding as it suppress weeds.

4. De-suckering.
Its important you remove all suckers on the base of the stump unless you are changing the cycle (rejuvenating ). 
This should be done before fertilizing.

 *NOTE:* 
‚óè Avoid spraying your coffee when flowers are open.It could result to abortion. Spray after 3-4 days after the flowers emerge or after the fall with a pesticide and a high NPK foliar.
‚óèFertilizer application should be done 2weeks after the rains. Don't be in a hurry or you could waste all through leaching. 
‚óèBackfilling should be done by end of the week.

By Agronomist Dennis 
Lead Agronomist, @Denaza Agroconsultancy .

kinyuadennis717@gmail.com.

Coffee Sample Roaster: Essential Tool for Quality Control

A coffee sample roaster is designed for roasting small batches of coffee beans (50 to 300 grams) to evaluate quality before large-scale roasting or purchase. It offers precise control over temperature, airflow, and roasting time, making it essential for highlighting flavor profiles and detecting defects.

Modern sample roasters come with digital interfaces, data logging, and repeatable profiles, making them crucial for quality control labs, exporters, and specialty coffee buyers. They ensure consistency and maintain high standards in the coffee industry.

*üåø ABFI TIP: Nitrogen Fixation & Rainfall ‚òî*

Did you know rain is a natural fertilizer? It adds nitrogen to your soil in two key ways:
‚úÖ During Rain:
Lightning breaks nitrogen (N‚ÇÇ) in the air, forming nitrogen oxides (NO‚ÇÇ, NO‚ÇÉ), which dissolve in rain and enrich the soil.
Rain captures atmospheric nitrogen, boosting plant growth naturally.

‚úÖ After Rain:
Soil microbes become more active, enhancing biological nitrogen fixation (BNF).

Leguminous crops (beans, peas, clover) fix up to 200 kg of nitrogen per hectare per year with symbiotic bacteria.

Non-leguminous plants benefit from the residual nitrogen, reducing the need for synthetic fertilizers.

üí° How Much Nitrogen is Added?
Rainfall contributes 2 to 12 kg of nitrogen per hectare per year, depending on intensity.
Lightning storms can add up to 50 kg per hectare in high-activity regions!
üåç Nature‚Äôs Free Fertilizer! Maximize rainwater benefits and plant nitrogen-fixing crops for sustainable soil health!

üìû ABFI | Agri-Biotech Farm International
‚òéÔ∏è 0713092858

05/04/2025, 22:56 - +254 795 220161: üá∞üá™Attention: All Coffee Farmers 

MAJOR BEST AGRONOMIC PRACTICES(BAPs) FOR APRIL 2025.(By Agronomist Dennis- +254795220161).
#The First  Coffee Nutrition Need# 

The main challenge with most coffee farmers in the World is the ignorance of proper timing (the 'WHEN ") for the important agronomic practices. 

Correct timing for the Best Agronomic Practices(BAPs) in coffee farming is key to the final results of coffee production.
Here are the major practices to do in your coffee farms: 

1.Desuckering.Remove all unwanted suckers *before* fertiliser and manure application in the trees you are not Rejuvenating.Remember,at this time we are interested with the berries.
2.Fertilizer application.The type of fertiliser is  determinant of the results of soil test analysis.Have your soil tested.Apply as per plant need(determine by assessing the berries available-how many kgs per tree).
You should apply 2 weeks after it rains well when the soil is moist and feeder roots are growing vigorously.
Apply along the dripline and 10cm away from the main stem. 
Use measures to apply the correct amount of fertiliser.
Applying too much fertiliser will result to leaching of much of it.Do split application. 
3. Manure application.Apply well composted manure (10L per tree).Apply along the dripline too.
4. Zinc and Boron foliar spray.These assist in berry expansion.Apply early in the morning when the temperatures are low or  in the afternoon.
5. Weeding and mulching.With moist soils,it will be easy to remove weeds in coffee farms. 
Mulching should follow after weeding,to suppress the weeds from growing.
6. Coffee planting.Having dug coffee holes(2ft√ó2ft) in January\February and Backfilling in March,we should now,with the rains do coffee planting.
(the foundation of all coffee farms) 

Issued:April 5, 2025

General Notice: This material is for general information to a large audience. Thus, results vary. Always contact a professional for support based on your specific needs.

üöú Unlock the Future of Coffee Farming with ABFI ‚òï

üå± Enhance Your Crop Health and Boost Yields with Nanocrop¬Æ Cobre! üå±
Introducing Nanocrop¬Æ Cobre ‚Äì the revolutionary solution for superior disease protection and enhanced crop production in coffee farming. This product harnesses nanotechnology to deliver unparalleled results, offering advanced protection and a range of benefits for your coffee trees.

üî¨ What Makes Nanocrop¬Æ Cobre So Unique?
Nanocrop¬Æ Cobre uses copper oxide nanoparticles‚Äîtiny particles that are 1,000 times smaller than the width of a human hair. These microscopic particles are engineered to penetrate plant tissues much faster than conventional solutions, allowing for deeper protection and faster absorption.

Why is this so important? Nanoparticles interact with plants at a molecular level, allowing them to target disease-causing pathogens more efficiently and provide longer-lasting protection. Because the particles are so small, they can be absorbed directly into the plant, working from the inside out to bolster plant health. This means that Nanocrop¬Æ Cobre not only protects against Coffee Berry Disease (CBD), but also strengthens plants, making them more resilient to stress, pests, and other diseases.

‚úÖ Why Should You Choose Nanocrop¬Æ Cobre?

Fast Action: The nanoparticles penetrate quickly, providing immediate protection and faster results.

Long-Lasting Defense: Protection against CBD, fungal and bacterial diseases, ensuring healthier coffee trees year-round.

2.Balanced Nutrient Supply

*The image above shows ABFI‚Äôs Berry Development Framework (BDF) ‚Äî a powerful schematic that highlights the full cycle of coffee berry growth, from flowering all the way to harvest.*

This framework helps farmers and farm managers understand the exact stages each berry passes through ‚Äî allowing for timely decisions, improved quality, and maximum yields.

Here‚Äôs a breakdown of the stages:
üìç ST1‚ÄìST2 (Perisperm Development)
‚Äì Early cell division and seed structure formation. Early detection and management here prevents yield loss right from the start.
üìç ST3‚ÄìST5 (Endosperm Development)
‚Äì The bean begins nutrient accumulation, defining both size and weight. This is the perfect window for targeted nutrition and irrigation to boost uniformity and volume.
üìç ST6‚ÄìST7 (Pericarp Maturation)
‚Äì The berry reaches final ripeness, locking in sugars, density, and flavor. Close monitoring ensures the harvest hits premium-grade quality.

18/04/2025, 23:22 - +254 795 220161: WHY MANURE APPLICATION IS IMPORTANT FOR HIGH PRODUCTION IN YOUR COFFEE FARMS.

Why Apply manure/Compost?When should I apply?At what rate should I apply?How to apply. 

Why?
->Adding compost or farmyard manure to your farm helps in addition of Soil organic matter(S.O.M).
->The SOM facilitates soil health through addition of microbial organisms,increasing water and nutrients retention capability.
->Retention capability of the soil for nutrients and water facilitates healthy growth of the plants.
->Healthier plants give high yields and will resist diseases. 

When and rate?
->In coffee farms,apply half a debe during the long and short rains.A total of a debe per year per tree.
->Apply 2weeks after the rains.

How to apply.
->Remove weeds and mulch under the canopy.
->Apply under the canopy leaving 10cm from the stump.Spread.
->Finally ,return the Mulch.

Note:
->Avoid raw manure as it destroys the roots as it decompose.
->If you haven't applied,you can still apply. 
->If you lack manure,use organic fertilzers.

Issued : 18th April 2025.

By Agronomist Dennis.(0795220161)

19/04/2025, 20:14 - +254 724 633722: In its native habitat in the Ethiopian forests, coffee grows as an understory plant, where the shade naturally regulates its flowering. However, when grown in full sun, coffee tends to flower excessively. Unlike many orchard crops that manage excess flowering through natural mechanisms like floral or fruit abortion, coffee attempts to mature all its flowers. This results in a biennial bearing cycle: one year, the plant produces an excessive yield, depleting its energy and nutrient reserves and often leading to overbearing dieback. The following year, the plant focuses on recovering its reserves, resulting in little to no yield. Therefore, growing coffee in full sun requires intensive nutrient management to prevent depletion and maintain consistent productivity. In countries like Brazil, Vietnam, and Colombia, coffee plantations are typically large-scale, and the trees are routinely uprooted and replanted after a certain period. This contrasts with our context, where coffee plantations often remain productive for over 50 years. In regions such as Ethiopia, India, and countries like Costa Rica, shade management is a common and integral practice in coffee cultivation.
19/04/2025, 20:25 - +254 713 555529: Practically ongoing extremes in weather patters has witnessed coffee bushes stressed by high temperatures. Those with regulated shade are ready to withstand the dryspell.
19/04/2025, 20:31 - +254 720 464900: Now from your research, which trees are these for our region and what is the spacing?
19/04/2025, 20:32 - +254 722 442781: There is a significant difference between a natural habitat, where quantity and quality are not primary considerations, and an artificial environment where coffee is grown for commercial purposes, where both quality and quantity are key performance indicators that determine commercial viability.

In coffee production, where we aim to increase the yield per tree to mitigate against fluctuations in global prices, it is essential that we advise farmers prudently. The biennial nature of coffee production often results from nutrient depletion coupled with insufficient replenishment. Current fertilizer recommendations tend to be blanket approaches that do not take into account the previous year's production, which is necessary for proper compensation.

I would like to challenge agronomists to stop following outdated suggestions without questioning their relevance. It is crucial to adapt our practices based on current knowledge and the specific needs of the coffee plants.

19/04/2025, 21:27 - +254 722 442781: This is a very interesting topic. Soil isn't a solid block; it consists of particles with air spaces that can be filled with water after prolonged rainfall, allowing water to infiltrate into the lower zones. Although trees have deep roots, their minor roots and root hairs are primarily concentrated between depths of 1 to 1.5 meters. In this regard, trees do not have the ability to manage moisture in the topsoil and subsoil to avoid competing with coffee plants.

A human being generally feels more comfortable in the shade than in direct sunlight. While humans can obtain vitamin D from brief sun exposure, coffee plants require 11 to 12 hours of sunlight for effective photosynthesis.

Wind exposure can be particularly detrimental, as it increases evapotranspiration (ET) during high temperatures. Therefore, a best practice would be to provide windbreaks by planting trees as border crops.

*Dangers  in deep planting for  coffee.* 
 _Avoid leaving a basin-like_

While seeming beneficial for stability,deep planting can actually harm the plant and lead to several disadvantages. 
These are inclusive of:
1. Root rot due to waterlogging.This eventually leads to death of plant.
2. Reduced Nutrient and Water Access.
The root system of coffee is in 90cm depth.Deep planting means that roots go down far from where the nutrients are .
3. Growth problems.
Deep planting leads to stunted growth and poor development.
4. Prone to pests and diseases. 
Weak plants makes them susceptible to pests.

 *Note:*
‚óèAvoid deep planting. 
‚óèSeek agronomic advice (@ Denaza agroconsulting we offer this service).
‚óèWe walk with you from land preparation, hole digging , backfilling ,actual planting to management.

28/04/2025, 10:29 - +254 713 092858: *Answer:*
At AGRI-BIOTECH FARM INTERNATIONAL (ABFI), the decision to spray nitrogen-based foliars during the rainy season follows a precision farming approach. We base fertilizer and foliar applications on past historical data, soil testing results, pH levels, soil cover status, and nutrient removal estimates from the last yield.
Each coffee harvest removes significant amounts of nutrients such as Nitrogen (N), Phosphorus (P), Potassium (K), Calcium (Ca), Magnesium (Mg), and Boron (B). Therefore, current fertilization must not only correct existing deficiencies but also replenish what was removed during the last crop cycle, and prepare for the current expected yield.

1. Direction (Precision Approach):

Before spraying, conduct a soil test and/or leaf analysis to verify if nitrogen is actually deficient.

Assess last harvest yield: For example, 1 ton of cherry removes around 40‚Äì45 kg N, 7‚Äì9 kg P‚ÇÇO‚ÇÖ, and 45‚Äì50 kg K‚ÇÇO, plus minor nutrients like Ca, Mg, and B.

Calculate the nutrient removal and adjust your program.

*Recommended foliar* during rainy seasons: Use a low-nitrogen, high-potassium foliar such as 15-5-30+Ca+Mg+B. This supports fruiting, stem strength, and prevents excess soft vegetative growth.

Spray Timing: Apply early morning or late evening during light rains. Avoid spraying under heavy rainfall or intense sunlight.

2. Direction (Speculative/Variable Factors):
Spraying also depends on:
-Crop Stage: Young trees (vegetative) vs. mature trees (fruiting).
-Tree Age: Younger trees may need more Nitrogen, mature trees need more Potassium and Calcium.
-Altitude and Climate: Higher rainfall and cooler climates increase natural nitrogen availability through atmospheric deposition.

*Rainy Season Effects:* Since rain brings extra nitrogen from the atmosphere, spraying additional high-nitrogen foliars without confirmed deficiency risks creating excessive, weak stem growth that makes the coffee plants vulnerable to disease and lodging.
+ If spraying is necessary:
For young, vegetative trees: apply a balanced foliar like 20-20-20+TE but dilute it by half strength during rainy seasons.
üå≤For mature, fruiting trees: apply a high-potassium foliar like 10-5-35+Ca+B+Zn to strengthen stems, improve cherry size, and enhance quality.

Summary:

> During the rainy season, it is generally not advisable to spray nitrogen-rich foliars unless a deficiency is confirmed through testing or severe visual symptoms are seen. Over-spraying nitrogen can cause soft, weak stems and negatively affect coffee tree structure. Focus instead on strengthening nutrients like Potassium, Calcium, and Boron.

28/04/2025, 10:59 - +254 795 220161: TO DO IN COFFEE BEFORE APRIL ENDS.

You ought to be doing these best agronomic practices in your coffee farms before the month of April 2025 ends.
Be keen not to fail on so doing.

1. De-suckering and maintenance prunning. 
Remove all suckers growing where not needed.
This will ensure the plant feeds well and pests will not find a place to hide.
2. Weeding and mulching. 
Weed to avoid competition for nutrients and mulch to avoid weed growth with the rains.
3. Coffee planting. 
Ensure you have planted the seedlings in the correct way and have the best seedlings.
4. Manure and fertilzer application.
Ensure  you apply manure and fertilzer in your coffee farms.For fertilzer application, you can as well apply in May. Check on the rains if you were late applying. 
5. Crop hygiene. 
Remove all dry berries due to CBD or berry moth to avoid spread.
6. Fungicides for CBD and leafrust.
Ensure you use preventive fungicides for CBD and leaf rust.
If 10% of the affected leaves has leafrust,use a curative fungicides as twiga hypox,tabibu etc.
7. Foliar sprays.
Use foliar feeds with high NPK, with Zinc and boron to aid in berry expansion.
