01/05/2025, 06:15 - +254 740 373485: Brazil, the world's largest coffee producer, has been experiencing significant challenges in its coffee industry, primarily due to adverse weather conditions, including droughts and extreme heat, which have impacted coffee production and driven up prices. These issues have led to decreased productivity, reduced exports, and higher global coffee prices(Gachagua/munya reform's has nothing to do with the current handsome pays
Here's a more detailed look at what's been happening:
Weather Impacts:
Droughts, extreme heat, and erratic rainfall have severely impacted Brazilian coffee production, leading to decreased yields and damage to coffee plants. 
Decreased Productivity:
In 2024, the average productivity across Brazilian coffee plantations dropped 1.9% from the previous year. 
Reduced Arabica Production:
Rabobank estimates a 13.6% decrease in arabica coffee production in the 2025/26 harvest compared to the previous cycle, while robusta production is estimated to grow. 
Rising Prices:
Global coffee prices have risen due to supply shortages caused by drought in Brazil and other major coffee-producing countries, reports NPR. 
Impact on Exports:
Brazil's coffee exports have been declining due to low stock levels and the impact of the drought. 
Farmers Turning to Irrigation:
Brazilian coffee farmers are increasingly turning to costly irrigation to address the impacts of climate change and drought(should this work, worrying should be our partner Brazil as developed country,they have more than enough manpower and finance to facilitate for the above,the government should ensure that we don't get back to the usual traditional days where coffee farmers were paid in cents). 05/05/2025, 18:13 - +254 713 092858: The cherry is likely in the berry development stage, following the December‚ÄìJanuary flowering season. At this stage, the berries are small and green, entering the crucial phase of pinhead to early expansion. This is the time when the coffee plant needs the right nutrients to support cell division, berry filling, and overall health. 
   ABFI recommend applying a foliar feed that is rich in Calcium, Potassium, Boron, and Zinc. These nutrients help strengthen the berries, prevent fruit drop, and support uniform growth. Products such as Calcium Nitrate with Boron or high-potassium foliar blends like 13:5:40 + trace elements are ideal. Feeding your coffee correctly now lays the foundation for a strong, profitable harvest.
*Given the rains, we already have Nitrogen from the Rains*

05/05/2025, 19:50 - +254 740 373485: What are the uses of potassium?
05/05/2025, 20:07 - +254 722 442781: potassium is crucial for the growth and development of coffee plants, influencing both the yield and quality of coffee beans, as well as the flavor profile of the final beverage. Proper management of potassium levels in coffee cultivation is essential for producing high-quality coffee.
05/05/2025, 20:09 - +254 740 373485: Then,do we need it for berry expansion?
05/05/2025, 20:09 - +254 713 092858: Yes
05/05/2025, 20:11 - +254 720 464900: No K here ama?
05/05/2025, 20:13 - +254 713 092858: At the berry development stage, potassium (K) is not only essential for berry filling but also plays a key physiological role in the coffee plant. One of its critical functions is regulating the opening and closing of stomata, which controls water loss and gas exchange. During the rainy season, when humidity is high, potassium ensures proper stomatal function, preventing excessive water loss and supporting steady photosynthesis. It also facilitates the transport of sugars (produced in leaves) to the developing berries, promoting uniform growth and sweetness. Moreover, potassium works in balance with available nitrogen (N)‚Äîwhile nitrogen promotes leaf and vegetative growth, potassium ensures that this energy is effectively redirected toward fruit development. A proper K-N balance prevents excessive leafy growth at the expense of berry quality, leading to healthier plants and a more productive harvest.

05/05/2025, 20:18 - +254 722 442781: Kabisa 
By the way, all nutrients are required all the time during the growing stages. 
The only exception is that some are needed more than the others during different stages .
Preparation before flowering and when the crop is carrying,  nitrogen is required the most ,  flowering, pin head and ripenning,  potassium. 

The fertlizer regime for coffee is designed according to the rainfall pattern. Otherwise, coffee should be fed throughout. 

On Foliars , there is no special time for Foliars, and every month is a foliar month, especially to meet trace elements requirements.  

NB.
NPK are major nutrients required by coffee in 12 months of the year . If any nutrient is deficiency at any single time , yields are compromised.

05/05/2025, 20:30 - +254 713 092858: <Media omitted>

05/05/2025, 20:31 - +254 740 373485: To achieve the best results,to my little or no knowledge ü´£
05/05/2025, 20:32 - +254 722 442781: It can't be stated better üëèüëè
05/05/2025, 20:33 - +254 713 092858: *mixing different foliars or overdosing the recommended application rate can have serious negative effects on plant health and yield.*  Also different company have different formulation, like gel technology, Nano Technology but to be precise:

1. Phytotoxicity (Plant Burn)
Overapplication or incompatible foliar mixes can cause leaf scorch, curling, or necrosis (dead spots).
This happens because excessive nutrients, especially salts, draw water out of plant cells, damaging leaf tissues.
2. Nutrient Imbalance
Doubling one foliar or mixing incompatible products can create an imbalance‚Äîtoo much of one nutrient (like nitrogen) may block the uptake of others (like calcium or magnesium), affecting overall plant growth and fruit quality.
3. Reduced Absorption
Some nutrients compete for absorption sites on the leaf surface. Mixing them improperly may reduce uptake efficiency, wasting inputs and reducing effectiveness.
4. Chemical Reactions in the Tank
Certain fertilizers or micronutrients (especially those with calcium, phosphorus, or sulfates) can precipitate or react, forming insoluble compounds that clog nozzles or become unavailable to the plant.
5. Crop Stress and Yield Loss
Instead of helping, excessive or poorly mixed foliars stress the plant, reducing flowering, fruit set, or even leading to premature leaf or fruit drop.

07/06/2025, 11:03 - +254 740 373485: Curative fungicides contain active ingredients that can eradicate existing fungal infections after they have already been established on a plant. Some common examples include tebuconazole, ciproconazole, azoxystrobin, and others.¬†
Key Active Ingredients in Curative Fungicides:
Tebuconazole:
This fungicide is known for its protective, eradicative, and curative properties against various fungal diseases, including grapevine rust.¬†
Ciproconazole:
Similar to tebuconazole, ciproconazole also exhibits protective and curative activity against fungal diseases, particularly in grapevines.¬†
Azoxystrobin:
This broad-spectrum fungicide is effective against several fungal groups and can be used for both preventive and curative applications.¬†
Dodemorph Acetate:
This morpholine fungicide is known for its systemic activity, providing both preventive and curative control of diseases like powdery mildew, leaf spot, and rust.¬†
Mancozeb:
A common fungicide used for various diseases, including blight, and is often combined with other active ingredients for enhanced effectiveness.¬†
Metalaxyl:
Another active ingredient often used in combination with mancozeb for broad-spectrum control of fungal diseases.¬†
Copper Hydroxide:
This fungicide has demonstrated effectiveness in controlling various fungal diseases, including stem canker in eucalyptus trees.¬†
Chlorothalonil:
A widely used fungicide for controlling a range of fungal diseases, according to Hort Innovation.¬†
Thiram:
A fungicide used for seed treatment and controlling certain fungal diseases, according to ResearchGate.¬†
Benzovindiflupyr:
This fungicide is part of a formulation that includes azoxystrobin and is known for its systemic activity and broad-spectrum control.¬†
Isotiainil:
This active ingredient, found in certain fungicides, establishes systemic acquired resistance in plants, helping them to protect themselves against diseases.¬†

22/06/2025, 10:00 - +254 722 442781: In Kenya, it is crucial to ensure that Ruiru 11 seeds for propagation are sourced exclusively from the Coffee Research Institute (CRI). Ruiru 11 is a hybrid developed by CRI, and the specific parentage and breeding process are proprietary to the institute. This means that any seeds obtained from Ruiru 11 trees, whether from a nursery operator's own farm or from neighboring farms, cannot replicate the original hybrid characteristics of Ruiru 11.

While the seeds from CRI may be priced at approximately 3000 KES per kilogram or more, this cost reflects the research and development that has gone into creating a high-quality hybrid that offers desirable traits such as disease resistance and high yield. Unfortunately, some unscrupulous nursery operators may attempt to cut costs by mixing CRI-purchased seeds with seeds sourced from their own Ruiru 11 trees or from other local sources. This practice not only undermines the integrity of the hybrid but also poses risks to the quality and performance of the coffee plants produced.

It is essential for nursery operators to adhere to ethical practices and obtain seeds solely from CRI to ensure that they are providing genuine Ruiru 11 seedlings. This will help maintain the quality and reliability of the coffee produced, ultimately benefiting both the growers and the industry as a whole.

22/06/2025, 16:01 - +254 722 442781: One issue that might be controversial here üòÖ is that you don't get any advantage by grafting ruiru scion to SL, and you can simply graft  Ruiru on Ruiru , Batian or SL .

22/06/2025, 16:56 - +254 740 373485: Resistance means that a certain variety has an ability to prevent a disease (in this case fungal CBD) establishing itself while tolerance means a plant has an ability to withstand the negative effects of a disease without significant yield loss .... Resistant plants avoid infections while tolerant plants can cope with infection BT due to human activities over time,we've turned the resistance varieties into tolerant ones, environmental change as well
22/06/2025, 17:01 - +254 722 442781: Let me give an example in Horticulture..Sometimes ago there was a variety of fine beans called Teresa, which was resistant to Rust . No sprays were done against rust, and it became very popular.  But within a period of 7 years , Teresa beans lost their ability to resist the rust pathogens . Probably through pathogens mutation or malpractice by the breeder .

24/06/2025, 20:01 - +254 722 593749: This is Coffee Leaf Rust. When applying fungicides....make sure that the pressure in the knapsack is so high such that the spray is atomised into fine droplets that appear as mist and ensure that there's thorough coverage on the lower epidermis or underside of the leaves. Kindly supervise your spray team.
Also consider using other approaches such as:
1. Good nutrition program that's well balanced and avoid overusing highly Nitrogenous fertilizers.... 
2. Proper canopy management so that leaves can dry quickly due to improved air circulation and enough light penetration.
3. Consider varietal conversion (top working) with resistant or tolerant varieties.
4. GAP's such as mulching, weed control and shade management also help a great deal.
NB: scout Your farm regularly or frequently and if in every tree you scout 10 or more leaves are affected then spring into action.

25/07/2025, 11:45 - +254 723 844860: *Abscission* in plants is the process where plant parts like leaves, flowers, or fruits detach from the parent plant. This natural process is regulated by both environmental factors and internal signals like aging and stress. It's a way for plants to shed unwanted or damaged parts, manage resources, and aid in seed dispersal. 
 *Here's a more detailed explanation:* 
 *What is abscission* ?
 *Abscission* is the shedding of plant parts. It's a specific process that occurs at a specialized zone called the abscission zone. This zone is a layer of cells at the base of the plant part where separation will eventually occur. 
 *Why does it happen* ?
1. *Natural Aging* :
Leaves, petals, and fruits eventually age and become less functional. Abscission allows the plant to remove these senescing parts. 
2 *. Environmental Stress:* 
Factors like drought, extreme temperatures, or nutrient deficiencies can trigger abscission. 
Resource Management:
By shedding leaves in the fall, plants reduce water loss during winter and conserve resources. 
 *3.Seed Dispersal* :
Fruits abscise from the plant, aiding in seed dispersal by animals or wind. 
 *How does it happen* ?
The process involves several steps:
‚Ä¢ *Cellular changes:* Specific cells in the abscission zone undergo changes. The middle lamella (the layer between cells) weakens. 
‚Ä¢ *Hormonal Control* : Hormones like ethylene promote abscission, while auxin can delay it. 
‚Ä¢ *Protective layer formation* : Before the part detaches, a protective layer forms on the plant side of the abscission zone, sealing the wound. 
‚Ä¢ *Detachment* : Finally, the plant part detaches from the main plant. 
 *Examples of abscission* :
1. *Leaf abscission* : The shedding of leaves in the fall by deciduous trees.
2. *Petal abscission* : The dropping of petals after flowering.
3. *Fruit abscission* : The shedding of immature fruits (fruit drop).
4. *Flower abscission* : The shedding of entire flowers.

2. Prune well to reduce microclimate.

05/08/2025, 09:53 - +254 722 338131: I may not answer for John but yes it's possible to separate coffee at the factory. I witnessed a coffee program in Nandi where the key goal was to increase women participation in the coffee value chain at leadership, production as workers levels in the coop. Male who championed the initiative in the program gave their wives afew coffee trees like 50 stems this allowing the women to be share holders thus giving voting rights during AGM's. The women were trained on GAP's to increase production per tree. The coop allowed women to bring coffee on certain days of the week and was tended separately up to sales. The success of the program was that that there was a specic buyer for the women coffee and bought at premium prices attracting more men to participate in the program. The very interesting bit was that the household incomes increased and the men consciously sold even what was their through their wife's MNO with the goal to increase family income. I believe the youths were enjoined with the women to encourage them since there was no particular buyer for youth coffee then. These initiatives have increased coffee production in both Kericho and Nandi counties.

Hope it helps abit before you get to know exactly where John's program is in supporting the women and the youth.
